REPUBLIC OF GUINEA-BISSAU
SOCIAL SECTOR PROJECT
Detailed Descri_tiog of the Social Action Fund Sub2roiec
Including Terms of Reference of Kiey Technical Assistance
1.    Introduction
1.    In February 1992, the Governent approved and recognized the legal position of NGOs and
formulated a law that regulates this sector (Decreto Lei dos ONG's Nacionais). This was the official
recognition of a process that had started in the middle of the 80s and that gained considerable
momentum since. In 1991, there were some 11 national NGOs and about 62 international NGOs
registered in Guinea-Bissau. They were working in a variety of sectors, both social (health, education
and training, culture and food support programs) and productive (agriculture, fishing, industry,
commerce and cooperatives). A recent list of these NGOs and their various activities per region nd
per sector has been elaborated by SOLIDAMI (SOLMDariedade and AMIzade).
2.    SOLIDAMI was created in 1986 as a public institution under the auspices of the Ministry of
Foreign Affairs and Cooperation (MINFAC). Its main objective is to act as an umbrella to coordinate
NGO activities in the country and to identify and support new initiatives in the different regions and
sectors. The organization is composed of four departments that promote, support, document and
administer the various projects and NGOS in the country. SOLIDAMI is supported by a variety of
donors. It disposes of a 'Fund to support small inidatives (FAPI)", that was created by a consortium
of some international NGOs (OXFAM, Solidariedade Socialista, NOVIB, and ICCO). Criteria
established to obtain FAPI's funds are in the area of production and credit, while they are only
available for local groups and national NGOs. However, internadonal NGOs have no access to these
funds.
3.    An evaluation by this consortium in the beginning of 1992 showed a moderate increase over
time of new initiatives to be financed by the FAPI-fund, while at the same time pointing to the limited
absorption capacity of SOLIDAMI to identify, elaborate and initiate new projects in the country. In
fact, during the first year FAPI used onle ECU 12.000 of which 3/4 in the rural areas. As
experience points towards the necessity to start slowly and prudently, so as to permit the organizations
working in the field to grow and keop control over eventual new initiatives. A period of several
years is probable necessary to permit a social action programme to develop from the bottom upwards
and to permit local control and community participation to take place.
II.    Obiectives
4.    The general objective of the Social Action Fund (SAF) is to support those initatives within
the social sector, that alleviate or diminiso poverty of the most vulnerable groups in the society.
Specific objectives of the Social Action Fund Unit (SAFU), that will be responsible for the exaction
of the programme are suggested as follows:
(a)    Define a Social Sector policy within the specific economic and socio-political context
of Guinea-Bissau together with other actor in this field (governmnt/
multilateral/bilateral/NGO'S);
(b)    Manage and control the Social Action Fund (SAF);



- 155 -
ANNEX 3-14
Page 2 of 5
(c)    Initiate and elaborate project proposals together with beneficiaries;
(d)    Provide technical and financial support for implementation and follow-up after
approval;
(e)    Provide financial and technical support both to grass-roots organizations in the
society, as well as to national and international NGO'S that are involved in the social
sectors;
(f)    Strengthen the participation of the beneficiaries in design and overall implementation
of the activities;
(g)    Monitor follow-up and progress through a pre-determined set of well-defined social
welfare indicators; and
(h)    Initiate as part of the general policy development some practical studies that help to
define the target population (For example a Household food security study to assess
purchasing power among low-income households or a study to develop practical and
simple indicators).
III.    Criteria and beneficiaries
5.    In principle the following criteria will apply when submitting proposals to be financed through
SAF. The proposals should be:
(a)    Linked to social problems and poverty alleviation;
(b)    Supportive to high risk groups in the society that gre directly affected by the actual
Economic Reform programme; and
(c)    Directed to groups of people that show interest and initiative and that are willing/able
to manage the funds adequately. The SAF cannot be used by groups that already have
a privileged position in the country (ponteiros/political parties).
6.    The most important beneficiaries of the SAF will be households below the poverty-line, that
are unable to assure sufficient revenue for their basic needs nor the access to essential services (health
and education). One could more specifically mention amongst others:
- Women (Single Headed Households/Widows/Prostitutes/Others);
- Children (orphans/streetboys/juvenile delinquents/others);
- Elderly people without family support;
- Handicapped persons both physically and mentally. A more detailed inventory of the various
organizations already working in this field should be made by an external consultant. He/she should
make a proper needs assessment and a more detailed definition of the target
population that has been most affected by the economic reform programme.
7.    Both grassroot groups as well as national and international NGOS can apply for the SAF.
Efforts to enhance collaboration between them will be considered positively.
8.    Detailed criteria and procedures for the approval of projects will need to be defined later by
the external consultant within the framework given in this annex. lbese criteria should clearly
delineate the difference between the FAPI funds (productively oriented and only for national NGOS)
and the SAF - funds (socially oriented and available for both types of NGOS). Overlap and ambiguity
in this area should be avoided.



- 156 -
ANNEX 3-14
Page 3 of 5
IV.   Organization and management
9.    In discussion with the Minister of Foreign Affairs and Cooperation, an organizational
structure for the SAF has been defined that allows for coordination, exchange of experience and
information,while at the same time it will assure relative autonomy in order to respond rapidly and
with flexibility to the needs of the target groups. To this end a Social Action Fund Unit (SAFU) will
be created within the premises of SOLIDAMI. This department will manage and control the funds of
the Social Action Fund (SAF). It will have an executive role. The SAFU will be headed by a
Manager/Technical Director for which task description and professional requirements are defined
below. The SAFU will be further provided with a locally hired assistant and the necessary support
materials under project financing. Detailed expenditure estimates have been worked out. A SAF
Technical Committee of the SAF headed by the Managing Director will meet regularly to analyze and
review proposals and decide on action and initiatives to be taken. The committee will be a permanent
structure that will assess priorities and progress. It is constituted by representatives from:
- MINPH and MINNE;
- National and International NGOS (on a rotating basis);
- SOLIDAMI Representative;
- SAFU Assistant to the Managing Director.
The Committee will meet regularly (every two-three months) in order to:
(a)    Review the proposals for new projects and activities;
(b)    Assess progress of the SAFU in responding to the needs of the deprived and
marginalised population.
10.   During annual review of the Social Sector Project, specific attention will also be given to
assess progress for the Social Action Fund . To this end annual reports (including budgetary
spending and forecasting) should be prepared and discussed, including the evolution of the pre-defined
indicators. At the same meeting an annual workplan with budget should be presented and analyzed.
In the third year of the project a short independent external evaluation is envisaged, if possible by the
same external consultant (on a two-month period).
V.    Personnel
11.   Within the SAFU, there will be a Managing Director, an assistant to the Managing Director
and support staff (accountant, secretary and driver). The bureau will be equipped with the necessary
materials (photocopier, computer, consumables, etc). It will be in the premises of SOLIDAMI so as
to allow exchange of knowledge and mutual sharing of experiences.

ANNEX 3-14
Page 4 of S
Ap,oendix
Managine Director
Terms of Reference
Responsibilities
- Administer and manage the SAFU as well as the SAF;
- Participate in the formulation, together with other actors in this field of a Social Sector policy;
- Stimulate promotion and divulgation of the SAF;
- Initiate and prepare projects and activities in the social sector;
- Support implementation, follow-up and evaluation of these projects both technically and financially;
- Participate in the training of staff in project preparation and implementation.
Reguirements
- Academic training in the social or agricultural field (sociologist, agronomist or other development
oriented training);
- Experience in the work with grass-roots organization and the NGO sector;
- Experience with the formulation of project proposals, their implementation and evaluation;
- Activate and dynamic character with good social communication capacities.
Assistant to the Managing Director
Terms of Reference
ResDonsibilitie
- Assist the Managing Director in daily activities;
- Identify felt needs among vulnerable groups in the society;
- Give technical support to grass-roots organizations and national NGOS in the formulation and
preparation of their proposals;
- Give technical advice, support and training in the implementation and follow up of these activities;
- Identify additional resources and support from other persons and/or organizations when necessary;
- Monitor and visit sites when activities financed under the SAF are being carried on to ensure
adequate use of the funds.



- 158 -
ANNEX 3-14
Page 5 of 5
Requirements
- Mid-level technical training in the development field, social and/or more productive-oriented;
- Experience with work with NGOS and grass-roots organizations in the country;
- Experience with project formulation and project implementation procedures;
- Good social relations and respect for marginalized and deprived groups.
SAE External Consultant
Terms of Reference
Res2onsibil ities
- Elaborate a detailed inventory of the various organizations working in the social fields in Guinea-
Bissau, multilaterally (UNICEF, ILO), bilaterally (Sweden, Denmark, etc) and NGOS (SNV, CECI,
etc);
- Elaborate a needs assessment of those most affected by the economic reform and suggest priorities
of actions to be developed.
- Elaborate a realistic work programme for the first year of the Social Action Fund Unit. Propose
social indicators that can realistically be included as measures of performance of the Social Action
Fund;
- Elaborate detailed criteria and procedures for the approval of projects within the framework of this
report.
Rauirements
- The consultant should have extensive work experience in the NGO-sector of Guinea-Bissau.
Preferably he should be acquainted with the social sectors and effects of the Economic reform
programs on the vulnerable groups. The consultant should speak and write Portuguese and preferably
should be able to speak Creolo.
SAFU Accountant
Terms of Reference
Job Description. In close collaboration with the PCU Project Accountant, the SAFU
Accountant will have primary responsibility in keeping financial accounts for the Social Action Fund,
preparing expenditures accounts, quarterly progress reports, and annual financial plans and
submission of accounts for audit. The SAFU Accountant shall also provide other necessary financial
assistance to the Managing Director nd the PCU Project Accountant.
Duration. Full-time employment during project implementation.

REPUBLIC OF GUINEA-BISSAU
SOCIAL SECTOR PROJECT
Terms of Reference of Proiect Coordinating Unit Key Staff
A.    Training and Management Technical Director
1.            The Training and Management Technical Director (the Director) will be responsible
for the planning and implementation of the Training component of the Social Sector Project, that
contains specifically the following types of courses:
(a)    In-service training refresher courses;
(b)    In-service training upgrading courses; and
(c)    In-service training medical professionals.
2.            The candidate will assume the following tasks based on available data:
(a)    assess health manpower needs of MINPH for each of the proposed upgrading courses.
(b)    assure the fulfillment of the various entree requirements of the candidates for the
promotion courses as summerized in the Aide Memoire of the Appraisal mission.
(c)    define competency skills of MINPH personnel at the various levels for the various
categories.
(d)    based on approved job descriptions and standard competency profiles of MINPH,
define the learning objectives for the various upgrading courses.
(e)    develop together with the Guinean staff the curriculum and the teaching skills
necessary for the execution of these programmes.
(f)    assure the official recognition of the courses at national and international level.
(g)    invite other institutions and personalities to participate in the various training
programmes.
(h)    assure correct working conditions for trainers and participants of the various training
programmes.
(i)    participate as trainer/facilitator in the various training sessions and seminars.
(k)    assess the impact and the effect of the courses provided in responding to the objective
of MlNPH to improve the quality of care dispensed by the health staff.
(I)    coordinate with the Director of the Plan/Studies and Cooperation Department of
MINPH the activities of the EEC component to assure EEC relevance with health
messages.
(m)   responsible for managing, monitoring and controlling the project funds allocated to the
Training component, and will work through the PCU Project Director on elaborating



- 169 -
ANNEX 42
Page 2 of 3
contracts and procurement (in line with World Bank's Guidelines) for equipment and
supplies necessary to carry out various training activities.
Rquiremqents
-      Medical Doctor, if possible with specialisation in Public Health and knowledge of the
health situation in Guinea-Bissau is a requisite.
-      Experience with the methodology in the elaboration of training programmes.
-     Interest in a wide range of issues related to public health and health services
development.
-      Experience in the management of multilateral projects.
-      Fluent in Portuguese and French, if possible in Creolo.
-      Good social relations with health personnel at the various levels. Active and dynamic
character with capacity to facilitate group activities.
Organizational features
The Training and Management Technical Director will be contracted by WHO at the request of the
government to execute the Training component and will be financed by the project funds.
He will be physically located in the premises of the WHO and have full access to its resources and
expertise, specifically in order to assure the contact with other persons and institutions and to promote
the exchange of experiences and knowledge.
Detailed financial and working arrangements will be elaborated between WHO and the Government,
subject to IDA's approval.
Financially and administratively, the Director will have the autonomy to propose annually a work
program subject to IDA's review and approval at the annual review prior to its implementation.
The Director will report to the Director of the Project Coordination Unit (PCU). However, he will
have full responsiblity for the technical implementation of the programme within the limits of the
agreed work plan.
B.    Procurement/Architectural Specialist (National)
1.     jbectiv:    Assure efficient supervision of the equipment and the project's structure; (1)
Verify adequate equipment for the projects's units; (2) Implement efficiently
the activities related to the structure of the project; (3) Support responsible
administration in the aspects related to the physical infrastructure of the
project.
2.    Functions:    To assist PCU Project Director in planning, organizing, programming,
supervision and control of equipment and structure to obtain the goals and
objectives mentioned in the document of Credit Agreement.
3.     Supervise the execution of specific functions of the structure and equipments.



- 170 -
ANNEX 4^-2
Page 3 of 3
4.     Manage the execution of the operational outline and presett the written report to tho directos
responsible for the project.
5.     Coordinate the execution of projects and establish adequate relations with the differet
jurisdiction, in the Ministry of Public Health as well as in the International Agency of Development
(IDA) with previous authorization of the director.
6.     Whenever necessary, select new locations for new construction, making sure that it is the
correct location with adequate conditions Cropography).
7.    Elaborate architectural programs for each one of the Health Units and Houses for Nurses.
8.    Elaborate preliminary architectural sketch (esdmate) for Health Units and Houses for Nurses
intended to be built.
9.     Select the professionals to hire for the execution of the planes of structure, electrical, sanitary
and details for the construction.
10.   Complete the books of duties to proceed with the opening of competition for construcdto
companies.
11.   Prepare budget to each one of the work to be executed (rehabilitation, substitution and
external work).
12.   Elaborate a methodology to select contracting firm to perform the construction job.
13.   Prepare terms of reference for the responsible person (manager, leader) to direcdy supervise
the work.
14.   Select the candidates and define the tasks related to supervision (execution control, staed
time, flow of work, price agreement, etc.).
15.   Control and fallow up on the contracts of supervision of the work.
16.   Maintain a permanent updated information of the project's activities.
17.   Any other task defined by the PCU Director.
Professional Profile:
* University degree in Architecture or Civil Engineing, validated ad recognized
internationally;
* Ten years or more of experience in adminision of Human Resources, architectural
drawing, construction administration and budget;
* Knowledge of the English and Portuguese langes.
Characteristics of the Position:
* Full time employment;
 Assignment will be terminated upon project closing date.
A: A4ENG(JZ1)

ANNEX 4-8
Page 1 of 2
REPUBLIC OF GUINEA-BISSAU
SOCIAL SECTOR PROJ
Sureision Plan ad Mid-Term Evaluat_on Criteria
1.           Bank supervision input. Regular supervision needs re described in the table below.
In addition, specific tasks such as review of progress reports, procurement and disbursement actions,
awdit reviews, etc., are estimated to require a total of four staffweeks of various specialists per
annum.
2.           Borrower's Contribution to Supervision
(a)    Progress reports wDI be submitted on a quarterly basis (in October, January, April,
and July of each year). They wDi comprise a summary of implementation for each
project component and financial tables, including revised cost estimates and revised
timing of procurement actions. The Project Coordinatig Unit (PCU) will collect
iniormation from the implementing staff (namely, the Training and Management
Technical Director, the Procurement/Architectural Specialist, and the Project
Accountants and the SAFU Managing Director) and prepare the reports.
(b)    Project coordinating, monitoring and evaluation will be the responsibility of the PCU.
(c)    Once a year, a joint Government/donors review covering all aspects of the project
would be held on the basis of a report prepared one month earlier by the PCU. The
joint annual reviews would be chaired by the Minister of Public Health. A
comprehensive review of the progress of project implementation will be held 18
months after credit effectiveness.
(d)    The PCU will be responsible for coordinating arrangements for IDA supervision
missions and for providing information to them. Officials from the concerned
agencies will accompany the missions on field trips; and
(e)    Mission briefing meetings on arrival and wrap-up meetings on the project will be
chaired by the Minister of Foreign Affairs and Cooperation with the participation of
the Minister of Public Health, and the representatives of the Social Sector Project
Implementation Committee.
(f)    Mission briefing meetings on arrival and wrap-up meetings on the Social Action Fund
(SAF) will be chaired by the Minister of Foreign Affairs and Cooperation with the
participation of the representatives of the SAF Technical Committee.
3.           Cofinanciers' Contribution to Supervision. [IF ANY] Cofinanciers will be consulted
on, and invited to participate in supervision activities, and will be kept filly informed regarding
TORs, Wido-memoires and results of IDA supervision missions. It is expected that cofinanciers will
paicipate in the mid-term review mission and bring complementary skills to the supervision
missions.
